  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'

  <span id="freeText10079414893291448539" style="display:none">A Christmas Eve snowstorm transforms one small town into a romantic haven, the kind you see only in movies. Well, kinda. After all, a cold and wet hike from a stranded train through the middle of nowhere would not normally end with a delicious kiss from a charming stranger. And no one would think that a trip to the Waffle House through four feet of snow would lead to love with an old friend. Or that the way back to true love begins with a painfully early morning shift at Starbucks. Thanks to three of today’s bestselling teen authors—John Green, Maureen Johnson, and Lauren Myracle—the magic of the holidays shines on these hilarious and charming interconnected tales of love, romance, and breathtaking kisses.<br /><br /><br />Alternate cover edition for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=B006MOW98E" title="B006MOW98E" rel="nofollow noopener">B006MOW98E</a></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142412145" href="/book/show/3213286-let-it-snow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/108756-shelley?shelf=youth">youth</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/108756-shelley?shelf=christmas">christmas</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40182210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3599274093209650747">It started off strong and got progressively weaker. Maureen Johnson was fun, John Green all right and Lauren Myracle dismal.<br/><br/>Maureen Johnson's story was super quirky and giggly and slightly ridiculous (in a good way). I liked Jubilee a lot, crazy as she was, and was amused to see a lot of my mother in Stuart's. It was just cheery, fun Christmas fluff.<br/><br/>John Green's kind of drove me nuts. I wanted to like it more, but I guess I am not that adventurous, because I kept thinking that the characters wer</span>
  <span id="freeText3599274093209650747" style="display:none">It started off strong and got progressively weaker. Maureen Johnson was fun, John Green all right and Lauren Myracle dismal.<br /><br />Maureen Johnson's story was super quirky and giggly and slightly ridiculous (in a good way). I liked Jubilee a lot, crazy as she was, and was amused to see a lot of my mother in Stuart's. It was just cheery, fun Christmas fluff.<br /><br />John Green's kind of drove me nuts. I wanted to like it more, but I guess I am not that adventurous, because I kept thinking that the characters were such massive idiots, but their idiotic actions were the only thing that created a plot. He kept referring to them as oh-so-clever, but they really weren't. They attempted to reach Buffy-level snark and sarcasm and really didn't make it. Also, the cheerleader thing got really old, really fast. I usually love him, so I was disappointed. <br /><br />Lauren Myracle's was so terrible and I hated every minute. Her main character was a self-absorbed whiny brat and I was stuck in her first person pea brained narrative for the entire thing. The entire thing was, admittedly, about the fact that she was a self-absorbed whiny brat and everyone was calling her on that fact, but her supposed transformation was utterly ridiculous. Also, the last chapter tied up all three of the stories and she massacred all of the characters from the other stories. Any wit and subtlety that the other two authors created, she destroyed. This probably would have gotten four stars if she hadn't written the final chapter and left me with the bad taste. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3599274093209650747" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2626153351" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2626153351" />
    <a title="Mary S. R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75831724-mary-s-r"><img alt="Mary S. R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597037601p2/75831724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2626153351?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary S. R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary S. R." href="/user/show/75831724-mary-s-r">Mary S. R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141349176" href="/book/show/49183047-let-it-snow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2626153351" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16604001436700753710"><b>3.5 STARS!</b> Cute snowy disasters and teenage romance :)<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“I always had this idea that you should never give up a happy middle in the hopes of a happy ending, because there is no such thing as a happy ending.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>Sometimes, snow can be a real pain. A naughty kid causing quite the chaos wherever she deems to grace. Ask the occupants of Gracetown—they can tell you <i>all</i> about it; because this year, it's snowing like it hadn't in half a century! Buried beneath multiple feet of snow, their cars stuck, tra</span>
  <span id="freeText16604001436700753710" style="display:none"><b>3.5 STARS!</b> Cute snowy disasters and teenage romance :)<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I always had this idea that you should never give up a happy middle in the hopes of a happy ending, because there is no such thing as a happy ending.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Sometimes, snow can be a real pain. A naughty kid causing quite the chaos wherever she deems to grace. Ask the occupants of Gracetown—they can tell you <i>all</i> about it; because this year, it's snowing like it hadn't in half a century! Buried beneath multiple feet of snow, their cars stuck, trains stranded, roads blocked, the residents of this little town are in for a hell of a time.<br><br>Because snow is also magical. Enchanting. A little bit of snow can make all the difference. Burying the real life and all the inconsequential things under a blanket of white, snow can change the way you see the world. It can make you take a path you never imagined. It can get you stuck, and, sometimes, that's all you need to do—get stuck. Pause, and truly see. Because sometimes, that's just where you need to be.<br><br><b>You just gotta let it snow.</b><br><br>Which is just what this book does. Three interconnected, hilarious, and charming stories about a snowstruck town, starting from one girl and continuing as a chain of reactions, Johnson, Green, and Myracle tell a tale of love, friendship, and the magic of holidays—which can change quite a few lives.<br><br><br><b><u>The Jubilee Express</u><br>by Maureen Johnson</b> ★★★½☆<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I felt so alone on that train…a weird, unnatural kind of alone that bore into me. It was feeling just beyond fear and somewhere to the left of sadness.<br>Tired, but not the kind of tired that sleep fixes.<br>It was dark and gloomy, and yet, it didn’t seem that things would get any better if the lights were turned up.</i>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <i>Storyline:</i>
</b> One brave soul ventures out into the storm from her stranded train, taking a risky shortcut with an adorable stranger, starting a maybe predictable story, but no less special in its own way and a great short read to lighten your mood on a tough day!<br><br><b>
  <i>Storytelling:</i>
</b> Precious and sweet right when it needed to be, hilarious the rest of the time, Maureen Johnson's writing is the reason it got 3.5 instead of 3. I am content :)<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I knew it was beautiful, but knowing something is beautiful and caring about it are two very different things, and I didn’t care.</i>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <i>Characterisation:</i>
</b> Perhaps the strongest part of this story were the characters, being well developed for a small town tale; Debbie (<i>the overly sweet, absurd, mischievous, and inappropriate mother</i>), Rachel (<i>the cutest five-year old that I oh wanna eat</i>), and Jubilee (<i>the crazy protagonist and comedian of the story, with thoughts that gave me so many laughaches</i>).<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>One person’s crazy is another person’s sane, I guess.</i>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <i>Relationships:</i>
</b> With absolutely cute and well-handled romance and the sweetest familial bonds, <i>The Jubilee Express</i> did it just right for the holidays.<br><br><br><b><u>A Cheertastic Christmas Miracle</u><br>by John Green</b> ★★★★½<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Something about me has always liked the drama and inconvenience of bad weather. The worse the better, really.</i>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <i>Storyline:</i>
</b> Three friends set out to win a race to the Waffle House. And the hash brown spoils. And the cheerleaders, ofc. You can guess how it turn out...I mean, c'mon, It's John Green. That man can write about the taxonomy of Brachychiton rupestris and I'd still read and love it. And no, that is not the name of As always, this was a whirlwind of madness, sprinkled with the warm company of crazy friends in a storm and a hilarious disastrous ride to the Waffle House. Poor Carla the car.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“YESSSSSS! WE JUST DID SUCH AN AWESOME JOB OF NOT DYING!”</i>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <i>Storytelling:</i>
</b> John is John and he does magic with simple words. He writes the most crazy events in such a chill and hilarious manner that is unique in its simplicity. Also, the gem of his writing is his conversations, and while Maureen Johnson spent a lot of time in hilarious and easy explanation of events, John Green is more a man of action who writes events and dialogue that are hilarious themselves.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I responded to this development with the kind of sophisticated language for which I am famous. “Crap crap crap crap crap crap crap stupid stupid stupid stupid stupid crap.”</i>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <i>Characterization:</i>
</b> The three friends (Tobin the protagonist, the Duke, and JP) were easily the best of the whole book. Even the sidekicks were masterfully managed and developed! The Duke (aka Angie) specially, with her hilarious, smart, crazy self peppered with the right amount of wisdom, make a mark on my heart.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Here is one of my main complaints about human consciousness: once you think a thought, it is extremely difficult to unthink it.</i>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <i>Relationships:</i>
</b> This tells all 😂:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Oh, I deep fried for you,<br>But now I weep ‘n’ cry for you,<br>Oh, babe, this meal was made for two,<br>And these hash browns mean nothing, oh these hash browns mean nothing, yeah these HASH BROWNS MEAN NOTHIN’ without you!</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><b><u>The Patron Saint of Pigs</u><br>by Lauren Myracle</b> ★★½☆☆<br><br><blockquote>
<i>“Silly girl, it’s not what the universe gives </i>us<i> that matters. It’s what </i>we<i> give the universe.”</i>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <i>Storyline:</i>
</b> The fate of a teacup pig falls into the hands of a lovesick barista sparking a tale that wasn’t anything special, to be honest. It was cute, unnecessarily dramatic, a little romantic, a lot more self exploration...and fine, really. It attempted to be magical but failed, unfortunately.<br><br>The reason I read it was mostly because I wanted to see what happened to the characters of the two previous stories, where the loose threads were gonna lead, and who was gonna meet whom. And for that, I enjoyed it. So 2.5/5 is the best I can do. If you're free and relaxed and wanting a fun read, this book is great; and this last story wouldn't ruin the fun of the previous ones if you look at it graciously and not too critically :))<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Christmas is a state of mind.”</i>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <i>Storytelling:</i>
</b> Lauren Myracle does not have a unique writing, or hilarious storytelling, or addicting turn of events, or anything noteworthy for that matter. But as my goal is to always get the best of each book, and make you enjoy it best, too, I'm gonna admit that Myracle had her moments and I did <i>awwwwww</i> on occasion and burst out laughing. The gem of this story was how beautifully and amazingly she used the two other authors'stories and wove them in her own!<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Shouldn’t I have some say over the endless thoughts running through my head?</i>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <i>Characterization:</i>
</b> The sidekicks and friends were not that developed even though this story was the longest of the three in the book—the author attempted to give them each backstories, meaning, and dimension, but didn't much succeed...<br><br>The protagonist, however, had a great character development and the story was mostly about her changing herself—in the beginning I was a little annoyed cause we were seeing everything from the eyes of a whiney self-absorbed drama queen, but it was intentional and her friends were not blind to it and pointed it out.<br><br><b>
  <i>Relationships:</i>
</b> In the spirit of positivity, I'd say—while there wasn't much to the romance—it was fun reading it run in background to character development for once!<br><br>In the end, I don't regret picking it up, if only for Johnson's Debbie and Jubilee, the puzzle pieces and coincidences and chain of reactions, and <b>JOHN FREAKING GREEN</b>—that man is a magician.<br><br><br><b>
  <u>Companions</u>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>Motion picture adaptation:</i>
</b><br>Released on November 8, 2019, it was fun for a free afternoon, silly and full of heart. The plot line differed a little from the book, and the changes both hurt and helped; for example making Stuart a famous singer was a nice addition to the first story and turning the Tinfoil Man into Tinfoil Woman and giving her more of a role was a great choice, while removing my little Rachel was not. The second story also was not as good as the book.<br><i>Audience rating: 46%<br>Critics rating: 81%<br>My rating: 65%</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1577875820i/28696841._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <b>Also by John Green:</b>
</i><br>• <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2346491407" rel="nofollow noopener">Turtles All the Way Down</a> ★★★★★<br>• <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2237362814" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fault in Our Stars</a> ★★★★★<br>• <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2237364060" rel="nofollow noopener">Looking for Alaska</a> ★★★★★<br>• <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2556001111" rel="nofollow noopener">Paper Towns</a> ★★★★½<br>• <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2611728719" rel="nofollow noopener">An Abundance of Katherine's</a> ★★★★☆<br>• <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2237369406" rel="nofollow noopener">Will Grayson, Will Grayson</a> (with David Levithan) ★★★¾☆<br>• <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2683641868" rel="nofollow noopener">An Imperial Affliction</a> (as Peter Van Houten) ★★★★★<br>• <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2683639959" rel="nofollow noopener">The Price of Dawn</a> ★★★★☆<br><br><b>

<div id="review_1856675018" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1856675018" />
    <a title="prag ♻" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29249069-prag"><img alt="prag ♻" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598781220p2/29249069.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1856675018?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="prag ♻" class="user" itemprop="url" name="prag ♻" href="/user/show/29249069-prag">prag ♻</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">somebody who wishes to die a horrible, painful death</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to prag ♻ by: </span>
      my inner john green fangirl
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29249069-prag?shelf=yam">yam</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29249069-prag?shelf=snooze-fest">snooze-fest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29249069-prag?shelf=oh-dear">oh-dear</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29249069-prag?shelf=let-me-down">let-me-down</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29249069-prag?shelf=yikes">yikes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1856675018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6621507933043046699"><b>Here's five reasons why <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33290383.Let_it_Snow' title='Let it Snow by John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>Let it Snow</a> is sentenced to a one star rating.</b><br/><br/>But first, it must be acknowledged that I did not suffer this <i>re-read</i> alone but was assisted by the traitor, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/49148508' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483162383i/21584518._SX540_.png' width='100' height='15' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/><u>
  <b>Offence #1: Self deprecating main character</b>
</u><br/><br/>I'm not saying everybody has to be confident and perfect all the time. No, I'm saying a well written character should have a personality <i>that extends further than feeling sorry for your <b>name</b> all the time.</i> The first story starts with about three paragraphs of rambling ab</span>
  <span id="freeText6621507933043046699" style="display:none"><b>Here's five reasons why <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33290383.Let_it_Snow" title="Let it Snow by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Let it Snow</a> is sentenced to a one star rating.</b><br><br>But first, it must be acknowledged that I did not suffer this <i>re-read</i> alone but was assisted by the traitor, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/49148508" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483162383i/21584518._SX540_.png" width="100" height="15" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><u>
  <b>Offence #1: Self deprecating main character</b>
</u><br><br>I'm not saying everybody has to be confident and perfect all the time. No, I'm saying a well written character should have a personality <i>that extends further than feeling sorry for your <b>name</b> all the time.</i> The first story starts with about three paragraphs of rambling about how <b>Jubilee</b> (who's the whiny narrator for the story) is such a <i>strippery</i> name although she certainly has nothing against strippers.<blockquote>My name is Jubilee Dougal. Take a moment and let it sink in. [...] I realize Jubilee is a bit of a stripper name. You probably think I have heard the call of the pole. But no. [...] My objection is that Jubilee <i>isn't a name</i>-it's some kind of a party. No one knows what kind. Have you ever heard of someone throwing a jubilee? And if you did, would you go? Because I wouldn't. Come to think of it, it might be interchangeable with hoedown.</blockquote>At this point, you might be thinking <i>this isn't annoying, it's funny</i>. Don't worry, that's what I thought too. But oh boy, when she brings this up <i>every</i> chapter, it gets on your nerves.<br><br><u>
  <b>Offence #2: PWP (Plot? What Plot?)</b>
</u><br><br>I suppose it's meant to be cute, how these stories are about teenage romances on Christmas Eve. I can assure you, it's not. I don't know <i>what</i> I was thinking when I bought John Green posters, but I believe it's safe for me to say: I fucking hate his writing. I assume his thought process behind writing a cheertastic christmas miracle was something like this: <i>Oh, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6442769.Paper_Towns" title="Paper Towns by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Paper Towns</a> is making millions. Wonder what would happen if I tweaked the characters a little bit and wrote the same story again?</i> <blockquote>"Gentlemen, may you travel safely and swiftly. But if you die tonight, die in the comfort that you have sacrificed your lives for that noblest of human causes. The pursuit of cheerleaders."</blockquote>The story summed up in three basic points:<br>a) 3 typical hormone driven male characters<br>b) 14 <i>hot</i> cheerleaders waiting for them (because what else would they want to do, apart from make out with idiots with twister in the middle of the biggest storm in 50 years?)<br>c) The Duke, who's not like other girls<br><br>What more would anybody ever want in a story?<blockquote>The Duke was just normal: she liked to joke around and talk about movies. She was much more like a person than other girls were.</blockquote><br><u>
  <b>Offence #3: Clichés overdone to death</b>
</u><br><br>Remember how I mentioned that girl<i> who's not like the other girls</i>? That's just the beginning.<br>In this bundle of short stories, we have: <br>1. Sweet guy who's heart has been broken by <i>oh you guessed, it, a cheerleader!</i> (Stuart)<br>2. The popular guy everyone wants to date who's just so perfect &lt;33 and also really boring (Noah)<br>3. Average male guy who talks about nothing but sex and girls in bikinis (JP)<br>4. The effervescent parents who call every ten minutes (Tobin's parents)<br>5. The girl who's so unique because she has pigs (Tegan)<br><br>There's also wonderfully written dialogue: <blockquote>Having no gathered my thoughts, I was finally able to eloquently articulate my feelings about the matter. "Crap crap crap!"</blockquote>GIVE ME A BREAK.<br><br><br><u>
  <b>Offence #4: Let's have an adventure at 3 am because that's what teenagers do!</b>
</u><br><br>I know, I know. I've mentioned this before. But dammit, that story pissed me off so much. Best friends secretly in love with each other? Check. Stupid ideas because HOT GIRLS? Check. Dirty talking to a car? ...check.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483165208ra/21584665.gif" width="199" height="199" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <br><u>
  <b>Offence #5: Stereotyping. Characters introduced only so they can be made fun of</b>
</u><br><br>I'm just going to complete this section with a bunch of quotes from the book, because there's really not much I can say.<blockquote>Could that be why he ate lunch with Nathan Krugle, who was definitely an outsider with his all- Star Trek, all-the-time T-shirt collection?</blockquote>Because <i>obviously</i>, somebody who loves Star Trek is weird. How silly of me to think otherwise.<blockquote>By making me his girlfriend, he demonstrated his belief in me, and I had picked up on his conviction. I stood straighter. He liked being seen with me; therefore, I liked being seen with me.</blockquote><br><br><br><b>I'm sorry, but this book was a cringefest.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="6621507933043046699" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1448997535" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1448997535" />
    <a title="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict"><img alt="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551124421p2/10717098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1448997535?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" href="/user/show/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict">Carol [Goodreads Addict]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142412145" href="/book/show/3213286-let-it-snow">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Carol [Goodreads Addict] by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/5701086-branwen-sedai-of-the-brown-ajah">Branwen Sedai *of the Brown Ajah*</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=anthology">anthology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=christmas">christmas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1448997535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7619435195936675277">Let it Snow is an anthology of three short stories, all tied together by a thread, written by Maureen Johnson, John Green, and Lauren Myracle. This book was a gift from a dear friend.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448303568ra/17120121.gif' alt='train gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>The Jubilee Express by Maureen Johnson</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448303568i/17120122._SX540_.jpg' alt='holiday village display: ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It’s Christmas Eve and Jubilee Dougal can’t wait to attend the Christmas Party at her boyfriend, Noah’s house. Her perfect boyfriend, her busy boyfriend. There are certain concessions one must make to date the perfect guy, right? She should just be happy to be his girlfriend. Bu</span>
  <span id="freeText7619435195936675277" style="display:none">Let it Snow is an anthology of three short stories, all tied together by a thread, written by Maureen Johnson, John Green, and Lauren Myracle. This book was a gift from a dear friend.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448303568ra/17120121.gif" alt="train gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The Jubilee Express by Maureen Johnson</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448303568i/17120122._SX540_.jpg" alt="holiday village display: " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It’s Christmas Eve and Jubilee Dougal can’t wait to attend the Christmas Party at her boyfriend, Noah’s house. Her perfect boyfriend, her busy boyfriend. There are certain concessions one must make to date the perfect guy, right? She should just be happy to be his girlfriend. But the day didn’t turn out exactly as she had planned. Her parents who were avid collectors of pieces to their Flobie Santa Village collection, which is a Christmas Village display, have been arrested in their attempt to obtain the latest addition to their collection. So Jubilee is put on a train and sent to Florida to spend the holiday with her Grandparents. Only the train didn’t make it. They became stuck in a snow drift in the middle of a blizzard in Gracetown. If that isn’t bad enough, there are fifteen cheerleaders on the train. To escape all the chaos, Jubilee gets off the train and treks across the road to a Waffle House. That’s so much better until the cheerleaders follow her there. She is rescued by a boy her own age that lives nearby named Stuart. Her time with Stuart teaches her so much about herself. And one kiss makes what once was the worst into the best Christmas ever.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448303568i/17120123._SX540_.jpg" alt="waffle house: " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>A Cheertastic Christmas Miracle by John Green</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448303568i/17120124.jpg" alt="Let It Snow - John Green: " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Tobin, and his best friend Angie who he calls The Duke and one other friend, are holed up at Tobin’s house watching James Bond movies. His parents’ flight has been delayed due to the storm and won’t make it back until after Christmas. They are enjoying themselves until they get a call from a friend that works at Waffle House saying that they absolutely have to get there because there is a group of fifteen cheerleaders stuck there for the night. So Tobin and his friends begin a crazy night trying to get to the Waffle House in the blizzard. But along the way, in the midst of all the chaos, he begins to see Angie as something other than one of his buddies. That maybe there was something there all along, he just wasn’t looking. This could just turn out to be one of the best Christmas days he has ever had.<br><br><b>The Patron Saint of Pigs by Lauren Myracle</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448303568i/17120125._SX540_.jpg" alt="starbucks in the snow: " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Addie is devastated. She has been dating her boyfriend, Jeb for exactly one year on Christmas Eve. But they have been having problems. Their relationship has been struggling. And then Addie did something dumber than dumb. Something she regrets with every fiber of her being. So she begs Jeb to meet her at Starbucks to mend things. But he doesn’t show up. It’s over. He doesn’t want to forgive her. On the day after Christmas when Addie goes to work at Starbucks with one thing she must accomplish that day, pick up her best friend’s new pet, a tea cup pig, she begins a small journey of self-discovery. I loved the ending of this one as the couples from the first two stories are all brought together in a very heartwarming way.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448303568i/17120126.jpg" alt="teacup pig: " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>These were three very heart-warming short stories that are sure to make you smile and will warm your heart during this very special holiday season. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425952445ra/13954015.gif" alt="signature" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="7619435195936675277" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/690807476?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="April (Aprilius Maximus)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="April (Aprilius Maximus)" href="/user/show/20658145-april-aprilius-maximus">April (Aprilius Maximus)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/18272314-let-it-snow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20658145-april-aprilius-maximus?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Janina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Janina" href="/user/show/3455554-janina">Janina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142412145" href="/book/show/3213286-let-it-snow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer126530314" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4069103762300522336">This is the perfect book to curl up with when it’s cold and snowing outside. It is one of those reads that just makes you want to snuggle up on your couch, a hot cocoa or tea in hand and enjoy the winterly atmosphere. In fact, the only thing missing for my perfect reading experience was the fireplace ;).<br/><br/>I don’t want to give too much away about the stories themselves because I think it is best to go into this book unprepared and let yourself be surprised. I liked all three stories, but <b>The Jubile</b></span>
  <span id="freeText4069103762300522336" style="display:none">This is the perfect book to curl up with when it’s cold and snowing outside. It is one of those reads that just makes you want to snuggle up on your couch, a hot cocoa or tea in hand and enjoy the winterly atmosphere. In fact, the only thing missing for my perfect reading experience was the fireplace ;).<br /><br />I don’t want to give too much away about the stories themselves because I think it is best to go into this book unprepared and let yourself be surprised. I liked all three stories, but <b>The Jubilee Express</b> and <b>A Cheertastic Christmas Miracle</b> were slightly better than the last one, <b>The Patron Saint of Pigs</b>. I didn’t like the main character too much there. Although the cute teacup pig almost made up for it … <br /><br />All in all, this short story collection is perfect for you if you are looking for a light and fun Christmas read. The stories are sometimes hilarious, sometimes sweet, slightly crazy, full of lovable characters (and pigs), provide you with a nice Christmas/winter feeling, make you laugh out loud and are just great to get lost in. I'm positive I'll pick this book up again some coming winter.<br /><br />A few quotes for you to enjoy:<br /><br /><i>Before I take you into the beating heart of the story, let’s get one thing out of the way. I know from experience that when it comes up later, it will distract you so much that you won’t be able to concentrate on anything else I will tell you. My name is Jubilee Dougal. Take a moment and let it sink in.</i> <br />(First page, first fit of laughter. The perfect start.)<br /><br /><i>I envisioned huge piles of the Elf Hotel flying off the belt, taking down everybody in sight. I had seen pictures of that Elf Hotel - it had sharp candy-cane spires that could easily impale someone. If anyone was ever going to be killed by an Elf Hotel, it would be my parents.</i> <br />(The whole story surrounding the Flobie Village was beyond hilarious.)<br /><br /><i>There is nothing about a bad situation that fourteen hyper cheerleaders can't worsen.</i> <br />(I have never even met one cheerleader. Yet, I can very much imagine this to be true.)<br /><br /><i>“Your mom calls more than a clingy boyfriend.”<br /><br />I responded to this development with the kind of sophisticated language for which I am famous. “Crap crap crap crap crap crap crap stupid stupid stupid stupid stupid crap.”</i><br /><br />And, not to forget, the teacup pig.<br /><br />(*sigh* I would really like to have one.)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4069103762300522336" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2770405224800265199">Sigh. Half of me wants to scream WORST BOOK EVER. UGH. BLEHH. MNEHH. AAARGHHH MY BRAIN IS BLEEDING. The other half is thinking: John Green, you absolute motherfucking genius. You managed to salvage this utter arse-crap. Well. Fucking. Done.<br/>As much as I hate chick-lit [and this is beyond chick-lit. it's like 300 pages of mushy, smoochy, splodge of chick-lit paradise], I read this because...oh fuck it, it's Xmas. I could barely get through the first of the 3 stories. It killed my brain cells, I sw</span>
  <span id="freeText2770405224800265199" style="display:none">Sigh. Half of me wants to scream WORST BOOK EVER. UGH. BLEHH. MNEHH. AAARGHHH MY BRAIN IS BLEEDING. The other half is thinking: John Green, you absolute motherfucking genius. You managed to salvage this utter arse-crap. Well. Fucking. Done.<br />As much as I hate chick-lit [and this is beyond chick-lit. it's like 300 pages of mushy, smoochy, splodge of chick-lit paradise], I read this because...oh fuck it, it's Xmas. I could barely get through the first of the 3 stories. It killed my brain cells, I swear it did. The John Green one was delightful, however. Honestly. I laughed. And the last one was yet another over-cheesy-brain-cell-murder-fest. I did like how it all came together at the end, but I must say that if it wasn't for the festive season [and this being my friend's book], I'd offer it up as a sacrifice to the gods of good literature, and maybe some people who've run out of scrap paper.<br /><br />The two stars are only for you John Green. If I could, I'd give you more but that would imply I enjoyed the rest of the book, which I most definitely didn't. So there. </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1834649428?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="abby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="abby" href="/user/show/44478099-abby">abby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/16081588-let-it-snow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44478099-abby?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44478099-abby?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44478099-abby?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44478099-abby?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1834649428" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7343295332986667316">If sweet and adorable got together and had a baby around Christmastime, it would be this book. I cheated on another holiday themed short story collection to read this one. No regrets. The three not-so-short stories in this book are loosely interconnected. In the first one, Jubilee is shocked to learn that her parents have been arrested in a black friday type shopping riot and that she's being shipped off to her grandparents' for Christmas. Her train gets stuck in a snow storm on route, and so sh</span>
  <span id="freeText7343295332986667316" style="display:none">If sweet and adorable got together and had a baby around Christmastime, it would be this book. I cheated on another holiday themed short story collection to read this one. No regrets. The three not-so-short stories in this book are loosely interconnected. In the first one, Jubilee is shocked to learn that her parents have been arrested in a black friday type shopping riot and that she's being shipped off to her grandparents' for Christmas. Her train gets stuck in a snow storm on route, and so she winds up meeting a guy named Stuart and staying with his family for the holiday. In the second, a group of friends are involved in a race to get to a Waffle House in the middle of a crazy blizzard. In the third, Addie is still reeling from her breakup with Jeb, one she totally caused. She's coming to realize that if she wants a Christmas miracle, she needs to change things about herself.<br /><br />All the stories are cute and humorous. However, the transition between them is not seamless. Maureen Johnson wrote her characters like they were in college, John Green like his were in middle school, and Lauren Myracle's were about on point. I liked the first story the best and could have easily read an entire book with just Jubilee and Stuart. The second story grew on me. At first, I didn't care for it because it reminded me so much of <i>Finding Alaska</i>, with his "too cool for life" characters, except the girl here (whose name is "the Duke" because apparently Green gets paid extra for horrible character monikers) is hardly a manic pixie type. The last story was the weakest, and the ending where they throw all three romances together winds up being a bit of a cheesy mess. That said, this is the perfect Christmas guilty pleasure read, and I could see myself coming back to it every year.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7343295332986667316" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_29346570" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/29346570" />
    <a title="nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/79453-nicole"><img alt="nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547514023p2/79453.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/29346570?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="nicole" href="/user/show/79453-nicole">nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142412145" href="/book/show/3213286-let-it-snow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/79453-nicole?shelf=romantical">romantical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/79453-nicole?shelf=holiday">holiday</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/79453-nicole?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer29346570" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6454845372905278590">Pretty much what you'd expect. Light, fun, festive. Had the feel of an ABC Family made-for-tv holiday special (which I love!), but funnier. And quirkier. Because John Green and Maureen Johnson are funny and quirky and their styles and characters fit together so naturally. While I like Myracle just fine, she feels like the third wheel in this collection of interconnected stories and leaving her to pen the final story and tie everything together was Let It Snow's major flaw. It was nice to see all</span>
  <span id="freeText6454845372905278590" style="display:none">Pretty much what you'd expect. Light, fun, festive. Had the feel of an ABC Family made-for-tv holiday special (which I love!), but funnier. And quirkier. Because John Green and Maureen Johnson are funny and quirky and their styles and characters fit together so naturally. While I like Myracle just fine, she feels like the third wheel in this collection of interconnected stories and leaving her to pen the final story and tie everything together was Let It Snow's major flaw. It was nice to see all the characters from all three stories come together, but I'm betting this would be a stronger read had the order of storytelling had been reversed.<br /><br />The appearance of Johnson and Green's characters throughout Myracle's story were the only parts of "Patron Saint of Pigs" that I didn't mind... but even those made me moan a little. Under Myracle's control, characters I <i>liked</i> and that, when written by Johnson and Green seem like actual <i>people</i>, sounded like bad acting. They just didn't feel authentic anymore. That was disappointing because I very much like her series of Winnie books, but these more mature characters still sounded and behaved like the tweens of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/357936.Eleven__The_Winnie_Years___2_" title="Eleven (The Winnie Years, #2) by Lauren Myracle" rel="nofollow noopener">Eleven</a>/<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/563322.Twelve__The_Winnie_Years___3_" title="Twelve (The Winnie Years, #3) by Lauren Myracle" rel="nofollow noopener">Twelve</a>/<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1030285.Thirteen__The_Winnie_Years___4_" title="Thirteen (The Winnie Years, #4) by Lauren Myracle" rel="nofollow noopener">Thirteen</a>. I cringed reading the shallow, meaningless things Addie had to say about Stuart (one of Johnson's characters) being Jewish. Her characters were just a bit... lame.<br /><br />Anyway, I'm getting caught in the negatives (which is what happens when end on the wrong note, Penguin!), but overall this is a sweet, enjoyable book. Johnson and Green are standout authors in their genre. They write characters that sound like people I know and want to hang out with. Johnson, in particular, was laugh out loud funny even and Green made something really fun happen with a car for the third time (or possibly fourth, but I haven't read <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/99561.Looking_for_Alaska" title="Looking for Alaska by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Looking for Alaska</a>
</i>, so I don't know). Bravo! I'll be singing it's praises to teens the city over this winter.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6454845372905278590" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3038944889" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3038944889" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3038944889?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3038944889" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9305362657836081242">3.5 stars.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>Let It Snow</i>
</b> is a trio of somewhat-interconnected short stories about the highs and lows of love against the backdrop of a massive snowstorm.<br/><br/>In Maureen Johnson’s "The Jubilee Express," a girl’s holiday plans are derailed again and again. First, her parents are thrown in jail unexpectedly, then her train to Florida gets stuck in the copious snow, and she escapes the chaos of the train by heading to a Waffle House for refuge, where she meets a young man with his own troubles. But as i</span>
  <span id="freeText9305362657836081242" style="display:none">3.5 stars.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Let It Snow</i>
</b> is a trio of somewhat-interconnected short stories about the highs and lows of love against the backdrop of a massive snowstorm.<br /><br />In Maureen Johnson’s "The Jubilee Express," a girl’s holiday plans are derailed again and again. First, her parents are thrown in jail unexpectedly, then her train to Florida gets stuck in the copious snow, and she escapes the chaos of the train by heading to a Waffle House for refuge, where she meets a young man with his own troubles. But as if all Jubilee experienced wasn't enough, she must deal with the apparent disinterest of her seemingly perfect boyfriend, which she doesn't quite understand. It makes for quite a holiday!<br /><br />John Green’s "A Cheertastic Christmas," told with Green’s trademark these-characters-are-more-erudite-than-me style, follows a group of friends trying to get to a Waffle House in the midst of the storm because of the unexpected appearance of a troop of cheerleaders seeking escape from their train. (This appeals to two of the three friends.) However, their mission to make it to the Waffle House before other invited males is foiled by the elements, their rivals, and the changing dynamics in their group of three.<br /><br />In "The Patron Saint of Pigs," Lauren Myracle tells the story of Addie, a girl despondent about the end of her relationship (her fault). But the thing is, Addie could use a serious lesson in putting the needs of others first. It takes a strange customer and a teacup pig to help her find her way.<br /><br />I don’t tend to read a ton of holiday books but this book (and these authors) really tempted me. Johnson’s story is the most straightforward and is therefore my favorite. Green’s is truly madcap and funny, and I really do love the way he writes even if his characters are funnier than nearly every adult I know, but there is only so much zaniness I can take in a story. It's literally a caper. <br /><br />Myracle’s story had too many disparate parts that didn’t quite come together for me, and I felt as if everyone was trying too hard. It was an interesting concept but at one point there were so many characters in the story that I was quite confused.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Let It Snow</i>
</b> was a very quick, fun read and it definitely put me in the spirit of the holidays, even if I’m hoping the "wintry mix" forecast for early next week here passes us by. They've also adapted the book into a Netflix movie which premieres November 8.<br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com</a>.<br /><br />You can follow me on Instagram at <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the.bookishworld.of.yrralh/" target="”_blank”" rel="nofollow noopener"> https://www.instagram.com/the.bookishworld.of.yrralh/.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9305362657836081242" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="oliviasbooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks"><img alt="oliviasbooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257619306p2/2843533.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/74801377?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="oliviasbooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="oliviasbooks" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks">oliviasbooks</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer74801377" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2733014893467067435">(ca. 2009/03/23:) Three snowy stories by different authors melted into a satisfying whole. Yes, I think, I like it! I have finished the first story "Jubilee Line" by Maureen Johnson (great style, by the way. Funny, a little crazy, a little romantic.) and started the second one, "Cheertastic Christmas Miracle" by John Green. After a few pages I thought: "Wait, another Waffle House in the middle of nowhere? These guys know a heartbroken boy named Stuart Weintraub? Ha, this is the protagonist from </span>
  <span id="freeText2733014893467067435" style="display:none">(ca. 2009/03/23:) Three snowy stories by different authors melted into a satisfying whole. Yes, I think, I like it! I have finished the first story "Jubilee Line" by Maureen Johnson (great style, by the way. Funny, a little crazy, a little romantic.) and started the second one, "Cheertastic Christmas Miracle" by John Green. After a few pages I thought: "Wait, another Waffle House in the middle of nowhere? These guys know a heartbroken boy named Stuart Weintraub? Ha, this is the protagonist from story one!" The stories are set at the same time: Christmas Eve - meaning, that possibly all three plots are happening simultaneously and touch here and there - although they have been written by different people. I simply love the idea and look forward to find out, who the last main character (story by Lauen Myracle) will be (maybe gentle Jeb with his broken mobile phone lost in a snow storm?) and how things will work out in the Waffle House in Gracetown. <br /><br />P.S. (2009/03/25): I was right. The third story is about Jeb and Addie and contains an end that ties all loose strands. I liked the first story best, though.<br /><br />P.S. (2010/12/04): I had a perfect snuggle-up time rereading "Let it Snow" with snow falling gracefully outside. I will reread it again some future winter. A teacup pig belongs into the category "pets-that-even-Olivia-finds-somewhat-cute" which contains squirrels and seahorses and cats when they are youngish.<br /><br />2014/12/29: Also the second re-read has been a both entertaining and ronantically heart-warming experience with a dusting of awe because the three narrations fit so seamlessly together without losing their individual flavor. I can tell that the book and I will meet again.</span>

<div id="review_670284033" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/670284033" />
    <a title="dyanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14780635-dyanne"><img alt="dyanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517428146p2/14780635.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/670284033?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="dyanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="dyanne" href="/user/show/14780635-dyanne">dyanne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142412145" href="/book/show/3213286-let-it-snow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14780635-dyanne?shelf=such-a-sweet-story">such-a-sweet-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14780635-dyanne?shelf=awesome-love-story">awesome-love-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14780635-dyanne?shelf=hilarious">hilarious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14780635-dyanne?shelf=all-nighter">all-nighter</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14780635-dyanne?shelf=love-the-authors-writing-style">love-the-authors-writing-style</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14780635-dyanne?shelf=badass-female-leads">badass-female-leads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer670284033" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10050635092687282325">This book, even though it is categorized as one book (singular) it should really be categorized as three books (plural) because although the stories within the book are interrelated, the writing-style and general plot of each story is unique and each could stand on its own. It only seems fitting to write three mini-reviews. <br/>Note: the review may get rather long and unwieldy. I apologize in advance.<br/><b>Section 1:<br/>The Jubilee Express<br/>3.7 stars</b><br/>Just a little taste of chapter one beforehand…<br/><i>..my name is Jub</i></span>
  <span id="freeText10050635092687282325" style="display:none">This book, even though it is categorized as one book (singular) it should really be categorized as three books (plural) because although the stories within the book are interrelated, the writing-style and general plot of each story is unique and each could stand on its own. It only seems fitting to write three mini-reviews. <br />Note: the review may get rather long and unwieldy. I apologize in advance.<br /><b>Section 1:<br />The Jubilee Express<br />3.7 stars</b><br />Just a little taste of chapter one beforehand…<br /><i>..my name is Jubilee Dougal. Take a moment and let it sink in.<br />See, when you get it up front, it’s not that bad. Now imagine I was halfway through some long story (like I’m about to be), and I dropped that one on you. “By the way, my name is Jubilee.” You wouldn’t know what to do next. </i><br />And so on. In this 117 page story, you find likable, interesting, <i>real</i> characters submerged into a plot that is sweet, funny, cheesy, just a little cliché, yet totally likable. <br />Sweet, funny, cheesy, likable. Those four words sum up the first story quite nicely.<br />What I liked about this story was how it flowed. Nothing seemed too out of place, and the ironic, extreme scenes didn’t seem too ironic or extreme until I thought it through after I finished the book.<br />Too think back on it now, another word that would nicely sum up parts of the book is ridiculous (but in a good way). <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Example: The fact that Jubilee’s parents got arrested on Christmas Eve because they were in a “shopping riot” that involved buying ceramic Christmas village pieces. Another example? The reason why Jubilee’s name is Jubilee. But you can read that for yourself.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Oh, just a little hint: Jubilee doesn’t hook up with the totally gorgeous guy who happens to sit next to her on the train. In fact, that totally gorgeous guy has a girlfriend who turns up later in the book. But more on that later. <br />Moving on…<br /><b> Section 2:<br />A Cheertastic Christmas Miracle<br />4.5 Stars </b><br />First of all, I love you John Green. Thank you, thank you, thank you for simply existing. No pressure, but I’m counting on a new book coming out within the next year and surpassing the brilliance of <u>The Fault in our Stars</u>. Again, no pressure. <br />Let’s get a taste of what the beginning of this story is like.<br /><i> “Tobin,” Mom said disapprovingly. She wasn’t a particularly funny person. It suited her professionally- I mean, you don’t want your cancer surgeon to walk into the examination room and be like, “Guy walks into a bar. Bartender says, ‘What’ll you have?’ And the guy says, ‘Whaddya got?’And the bartender says, ‘I don’t know what I got, but I know what you got: Stage IV melanoma.’”</i><br />So what words sum up this book? I’m thinking something along the lines of <i>John Greenish</i>. If you have already read a book by John Green, you know what to expect. Witty, lovable, comical, adventurous, sweet books that are realistic in ways that even words can’t sum up (purely a personal opinion, but when it comes to John Green I can’t help but gush). <br />It wasn’t John Green’s best, but the characters, the minor yet still interesting plot, and the humor scattered throughout was brilliant, and I thoroughly enjoyed every minute of it.<br />Note: it would’ve gotten a four stars except the main character mentioned <u>The Book Thief</u> as one of his favorite books on p. 192 and that bumped it up by .5 stars<br /><b>Section 3:<br />The Patron Saint of Pigs<br />1.3 Stars</b><br />Oh dear. Okay, I’m really going to try not to curse in this review because it’s not professional. <br />But…<br />This story is complete waste of time and paper. <br />I will not insult or name-call the author, because I do not know her, but I feel I have the right to complain about the story. <br />Again, let’s have a little taste of the beginning, shall we?<br /><i> “You’ve been on the phone with either Dorrie or Tegan pretty much twenty-four/seven.”<br />“You’ve been listening to my calls?” I cried. “You eavesdropped on your own daughter?!”<br />“It’s hardly ‘eavesdropping’ if you have no choice.”<br />I gaped at her. She pretended to be so motherly in her Christmas apron, making Cherries Jubilee from an old family recipe, when really she was… she was…<br />Well, I didn’t know what she was, just that it was wrong and bad and evil to listen in on other people’s conversations. <br />“And <b>don’t</b> say ‘twenty four/seven,’” I said. “You’re too old to say ‘twenty-four/seven.’”</i><br />And…so on.<br />Gosh, I really hated this story.<br />My main problemos:<br />1)	The main character. Addie. The story is from her perspective and there couldn’t be a more shallow, narrow-minded, annoying, bitchy character in existence. Oh, and remember the totally gorgeous guy at the beginning of the review? He’s her boyfriend. I feel so sorry for him. But then again, he’s an idiot for liking her in the first place, so my sorrow isn’t THAT deep. <br />2)	The story makes it seem okay to cheat on someone if you apologize profusely and feel sorry for yourself afterwards. The main character makes a bunch of excuses why kissing someone that was not her significant other is okay, and the infuriating thing is that her boyfriend seems to buy it. Okay, so forgiveness is a virtue but getting back together with one who cheated on you is taking it too far.<br />3)	The characters that were realistic and likable in the other two stories become warped and not so likable and realistic in this story.<br />So where does the 1.3 stars come in? The one star was basically a pity star while the .3 star is from the fact the author didn’t TOTALLY mess up the other characters John and Maureen made so perfectly flawed.<br />Overall? <br /><b> 3.17 Stars.</b><br />If you want an enjoyable experience, I suggest you skip the last story altogether. <br />Thank you for bearing with this long, unwieldy review to the end.<br />That is all. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10050635092687282325" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_486579592" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

I think this is one of my favorite endings from all of the books I've read since I was somewhat expecting all of the characters to meet at some point in the book towards the end, but never in my wildest dreams did I think it was going to wrap up so beautifully and I'm just so happy I waited till Christmas to read this book because it's totally perfect to read on a winter night eating some freshly baked cookies and just overall having a really chill time. <br /><br />This book's spine is reaaally used I mean I was so engrossed in this book I twisted and turned it so much I feel so sorry for it, but I was so enthralled I didn't even know what was going on around me! I wasn't conscious when I did this to me book, because I was so into the story I was seeing myself living the story on my own body. <br /><br />I think that these three authors made a splendid job in this co-authored book and i wish they'd do more! It came out even better than the one John Green did with David Levithan (Will Grayson, Will Grayson) and I didn't think I'd love co-authored books as much as I do! <br /><br /><b>2nd re-read December 20, 2012: 5 stars</b><br /><br />LET IT SNOW FOR THE WIN!!<br /></span>

<div id="review_1834964898" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1834964898" />
    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1834964898?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=finished-but-wish-i-hadn-t">finished-but-wish-i-hadn-t</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1834964898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11611415925883962785"><b> 2 Stars<br/><br/>Overview: </b><br/><br/>I read this because of John Green. Not even gonna lie. <br/><br/>I was hoping for three, fluffy holiday stories—like the summary promises. Instead this was just three choppy stories.<br/><br/><b> Pros: </b><br/><br/>It <i>was</i> cute, like it promised. <br/><br/>I think the main reason I’m giving this two stars is because, in a weird way, the writing wasn’t <i>bad.</i> It was quirky and humorous in all three stories, and I could easily see how all three authors wrote longer, more enjoyable fiction.<br/><br/><b>Cons: </b><br/><br/>No one had time to devlop. It fel</span>
  <span id="freeText11611415925883962785" style="display:none"><b> 2 Stars<br /><br />Overview: </b><br /><br />I read this because of John Green. Not even gonna lie. <br /><br />I was hoping for three, fluffy holiday stories—like the summary promises. Instead this was just three choppy stories.<br /><br /><b> Pros: </b><br /><br />It <i>was</i> cute, like it promised. <br /><br />I think the main reason I’m giving this two stars is because, in a weird way, the writing wasn’t <i>bad.</i> It was quirky and humorous in all three stories, and I could easily see how all three authors wrote longer, more enjoyable fiction.<br /><br /><b>Cons: </b><br /><br />No one had time to devlop. It felt like I was just thrust into different stories and told <i>so</i> so much about the characters and their lives. Or in the case of John Green’s story, I was just thrust in the middle of a friend group who kept shouting inside jokes at each other. I didn’t understand anything, and I didn’t really enjoy it.<br /><br /><b>In Conclusion: </b><br /><br />I think if each of these stories had been their own book, and had time to work with all the characters and plots, I would have enjoyed them. As it was, it just felt confusing and overstuffed. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11611415925883962785" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
