<div id="review_1467762436" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1467762436" />
    <a title="Giulia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16078869-giulia"><img alt="Giulia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443715060p2/16078869.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1467762436?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giulia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giulia" href="/user/show/16078869-giulia">Giulia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780142414996" href="/book/show/6883008-let-it-snow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16078869-giulia?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16078869-giulia?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16078869-giulia?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16078869-giulia?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16078869-giulia?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1467762436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3156065093592727145"><i><b>3.75 stars</b>. <br/>I'm so busy at the moment that I don't have time to write a proper review. <br/>But I really enjoyed it. It was a light read filled with Christmas-y feels and love. Perfect for the holidays if you ask me, when everyone's so busy they don't have time to actually <i>read</i>.;)<br/><br/>*Review to come!*</i><br/>-------------------------------------------------------------------------------<br/>Okay, let's start by saying that I am that person who starts listening to Christmas music in November. As December approaches, I</span>
  <span id="freeText3156065093592727145" style="display:none"><i><b>3.75 stars</b>. <br>I'm so busy at the moment that I don't have time to write a proper review. <br>But I really enjoyed it. It was a light read filled with Christmas-y feels and love. Perfect for the holidays if you ask me, when everyone's so busy they don't have time to actually <i>read</i>.;)<br><br>*Review to come!*</i><br>-------------------------------------------------------------------------------<br>Okay, let's start by saying that I am that person who starts listening to Christmas music in November. As December approaches, I become quite obsessed with everything red, gold and dark green, I turn into a walking Christmas impersonation. (That's not entirely correct, but I hope you get the idea. ) I love Christmas and if you don't then<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450643918ra/17450982.gif" alt="xmas" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, this year I decided to transfer my Christmas spirit needs into a bookish form. What does that mean? Not only I did listen to Christmas music and watched every movie with a hint of festivities in it, but I also dedicated part of this moth to read a few books with a Christmas theme. And the first one was <b>Let It Snow</b>. <br><br><b>Let It Snow</b> is a collection of three stories from three different authors: Maureen Johnson, John Green and Lauren Myracle. I have to admit I didn't read anything from them before <s>(shame on me)</s>, so I was new to their writing and way of developing characters and plots. I wasn't blown away by any of the stories, after all they were just about 100 pages each I don't think there's a lot to work on, but I was positively impressed by their overall dedication in turning this book into a "you must read it if it's Christmas" kind of book.<br><br>Now, onto the actual story. The three stories revolve all around the same background informations. It's Christmas Eve and the weather outside id frightful <i>(I told you I am obsessed)</i>. There is a blizzard outside, the kind of one you need to stay inside with a book, a chocolate mug and a cozy blanket near the fire, not the kind during which you go outside throwing snowballs at friends and neighbors. It was that bad. Even a train had to stop its route (luckily near a residential area) and the only shops open are a Waffle House and a Starbucks. <br>What would you do if you were stuck in a train/at home/at a Starbucks during a blizzard?<br>Let's see what the protagonists of the stories would do. * I don't want to say a lot about the single stories because I would prefer not to ruin it for you as I encourage you all to read one or all during this week. Anyway, I hope not to give too many details away. *<br><br><b>The Jubilee Express</b> by <b>Maureen Johnson</b><br>I think this story was my favorite. It is about a girl named Jubilee whose parents are obsessed with the Flobie Village. I personally didn't know what the thing was or if the hype was real. Turns out it wasn't that real, but Maureen made totally plausible. Well, it turns out that that famous Flobie Santa Village is going to change her life. Even though she is stuck on a train full of cheerleaders in the middle of a blizzard near a town called Gracetown, she doesn't lose her spirit. Jubilee decides to go out of the train and walk into the Waffle House nearby. Who is she going to meet? Where is she going to spend her Christmas Eve and the next days with? Will she find love? <br>I thought Maureen's writing was lively, fun and easy to read. I really enjoyed how the plot developed and Jubilee's character was one you could identify with. Also, the ending was the sweetest. Call me cheesy, but whatever. I am who I am, I won't apologize. Am I romantic? Yes. Do I like happy endings? Absolutely. Do I believe in love at first sight? Only if I can see it. And that is what happened in this story. I was able to actually SEE those two cuties fall for each other, even if their past experiences weren't forgiving with their heart.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Debbie had to get up and slice me a thick piece of cake before she could answer. And I do mean thick. Harry Potter volume seven thick. I could have knocked out a burglar with this piece of cake. Once I tasted it, though, it seemed just the right size.”</i>
</b><br><br><b>A Cheertastic Christmas Miracle</b> by <b>John Green</b><br>This story is set after the beginning of the first one. That means that it isn't Christmas Eve morning or afternoon, it was evening and late night. I didn't enjoy it as much as the Maureen Johnson one, but I was pleased by the ending.<br>Take three friends (two boys and a girl) marathoning the James Bond movies when a fourth friend working the night shift at Waffle House calls them saying it's URGENT. What do you do? You answer of course. So, they have to go there about immediately bringing with them a twister. Cheerleaders are waiting for it and everyone needs to hurry because they told him so. Boys will be boys. Give them a bunch of cheerleaders (with no offense to them) and they will lose their mind. In fact, the three Waffle House employees all called their mutual friends to bring a twister as fast as they can. They will only let in, the group of friends who arrive first. So our three James Bond's lovers have to hurry asap. During their perilous adventure which includes its fair share of ups and downs, they come to the realization that it isn't about the destination, but about the journey. They will, in fact, learn how to gather their forces against the enemies and to distinguish what's real to what's just an idea in their mind. Is there love involved? Yes. Will our heroes manage to be the winners of the Twister Request? I won't tell you, but if you read above I like happy endings so... Ah I almost forgot to mention that my favorite aspect of this story was the friendship. #squadgoals <br><br><b>
  <i>“We just did an awesome job of not dying.”</i>
</b><br><br><b>The Patron of Saint Pigs</b> by <b>Lauren Myracle</b><br>If you are wondering why there's a mention of pigs in a supposedly Christmas story, well, don't worry, I was wondering too. But at the end it all made sense. Actually the fact that at the end it all made sense (all characters, events, people, places, actions) was my favorite feature of this story.<br>However let's start by stating that the main protagonist was a bit annoying. She was quite pretentious and I didn't enjoy how she treated her friends. She was selfish. BUT. There are reason why she behaves like she does and whether or not I liked her, the ending made it all acceptable. She broke up with her boyfriend because she kissed another boy. <i>I hate that.</i> She wrote him an e-mail hoping for him to come back, giving him a date and a place. <i>I am not fond of that.</i> She and one her two best friends decide to buy a teacup piglet to the other best friend. <i>That's cute.</i> These were the vibes I got from the story: nah, meh, okay, cute. But that ending, wow, I was so happy about it. It was so adorable. All the previous characters made an appearance at the Starbucks this annoying girl works at and the ending gave a proper end to each individual story. So. Cute. <br><br><b>
  <i>“Christmas is never over,unless you want it to be... Christmas is a state of mind.”</i>
</b><br><br>Overall I guess it was the book I was looking for. The Christmas vibes weren't too prominent, but added the perfect amount of fluffy feelings. You could hear jingle bells playing in your head. It made you wish for snow. Those friendships made you miss your own friends. It is a perfect read for the festivities and I highly recommend it if you are looking for something to fill you Christmas need. It is just so cute and adorable! Obviously don't set your expectations high because, let's be real, these stories are not masterpieces. But I really really enjoyed them! <br>Also, teacup pig. You're welcome.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450714416i/17459228.jpg" alt="teacup-pig" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In honor of this book title, here's a gif for snow/winter/Christmas lovers out there.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416421519ra/11961861.gif" alt="letitsnow" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>Fun Fact.</u> I wrote the word <i>Christmas</i> 16 times in 1 review. I am not even sure if I still recognize that word. <s>who I am kidding I will recognize it everywhere</s>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3156065093592727145" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_40970213" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40970213" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/202724-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601676054p2/202724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40970213?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/202724-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142412145" href="/book/show/3213286-let-it-snow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=christmas">christmas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=youngadult">youngadult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=all-timefavorites">all-timefavorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40970213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7740782258517634104">Three of today's top YA authors have written intertwining novellas set on Christmas in a small town in North Carolina. A Waffle House figures big, and so does Starbucks, a train, a blizzard, and a teacup pig. I can't say any more without ruining things, but this book is a Christmas gift in itself: funny and well-written, not to mention romantic, all three are equally strong!<br/><br/>Reread, Christmas 2012: Love this book every time! I think The Jubilee Express might be my favorite, by a narrow margin.<br/><br/>Rer</span>
  <span id="freeText7740782258517634104" style="display:none">Three of today's top YA authors have written intertwining novellas set on Christmas in a small town in North Carolina. A Waffle House figures big, and so does Starbucks, a train, a blizzard, and a teacup pig. I can't say any more without ruining things, but this book is a Christmas gift in itself: funny and well-written, not to mention romantic, all three are equally strong!<br /><br />Reread, Christmas 2012: Love this book every time! I think The Jubilee Express might be my favorite, by a narrow margin.<br /><br />Reread, Christmas 2013: I want a teacup pig.<br /><br />Reread, Christmas 2014: Really starting to wonder how this was written. Did they brainstorm it together? Did Maureen write her story, send it to John, who sent them to Lauren? Very curious.<br /><br />Reread, Christmas 2017: Totally assuming that Maureen wrote her story, then passed it to John, who added his part, who passed it to Lauren, who finished it off. Each story is unique, and yet they are seamless at the same time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7740782258517634104" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2503000162" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2503000162" />
    <a title="Lara (Bookish_turtle)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64318901-lara-bookish-turtle"><img alt="Lara (Bookish_turtle)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512780612p2/64318901.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3167955990" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3167955990" />
    <a title="Tamoghna Biswas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/97513431-tamoghna-biswas"><img alt="Tamoghna Biswas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580746459p2/97513431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3167955990?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tamoghna Biswas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tamoghna Biswas" href="/user/show/97513431-tamoghna-biswas">Tamoghna Biswas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/21243178-let-it-snow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97513431-tamoghna-biswas?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97513431-tamoghna-biswas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3167955990" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17678067023244637656"><br/><b>
  <i>**3.5 stars**<br/><br/>“It’s always awkward when someone doesn’t realize you’re joking and devotes thought time to what you’ve said. Double that when the person is wearing tinfoil.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Many collaborations fail drastically, and some succeed dramatically. And this one comes somewhere in the middle, seeing John Green is one of the hot favorites of these times.<br/><br/>I was apprehensive enough before picking this one up wing to my previous unpleasant experiences with YA novels. However, this anthology is quite surpri</span>
  <span id="freeText17678067023244637656" style="display:none"><br /><b>
  <i>**3.5 stars**<br /><br />“It’s always awkward when someone doesn’t realize you’re joking and devotes thought time to what you’ve said. Double that when the person is wearing tinfoil.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Many collaborations fail drastically, and some succeed dramatically. And this one comes somewhere in the middle, seeing John Green is one of the hot favorites of these times.<br /><br />I was apprehensive enough before picking this one up wing to my previous unpleasant experiences with YA novels. However, this anthology is quite surprisingly enjoyable for someone who really doesn’t like YA much! I picked it up on Christmas 2017, as the stories are on a Christmas eve with “biggest blizzard in fifty years” about to happen. The three stories in here are by three quite prominent authors and are designed so as to coincide with something of “heart-warming consequences” in the end, which they did, a bit too obviously perhaps for my taste. The plot, if we take it all as one suffers through several hit-and-miss, but end of the day I had overlooked them all the first time I read it. Nowadays teenage love is most of the time so wrongly portrayed that people like me, despite being a teenager always flee from them. (I don’t know why they do that? If they go on with teenage romance being all on drug, sex and breakups and still expect the other world not to misunderstand it, are they being anything more than hypocrites?) But this one is mostly “cute”.<br /><br />If you want to compare, undoubtedly John Green’s <b>“A Cheertastic Christmas Miracle”</b> comes first. It’s light, funny, and does its job perfectly in overshadowing the imperfectness, well, come on its just a short story. The characters are mostly as you expect them to be, and the ending is light-heartedly great. Then comes Maureen Johnson’s <b>“The Jubilee Express”</b>, in which though the <i>teeth-chattery cold-and-windy</i> setting is awesome, the characters are in the shades of black and white only, which does get pretty irksome at certain points. Lauren Myracle’s <b>“The Patron Saint Of Pigs”</b> is really much more flawed if you can ignore the teacup pig. An obnoxious protagonist doesn’t help with the flow, either, not with her ridiculous simpering. And again, if I talk about the ending, it seems like they are trying to “create” a perfectly happy ending for all. Bit unrealistic for my taste. Life isn’t that super-easy, bruh.<br /><br />Two suggestions. Even if you are from a place where it never snows, like I, pick this one on a holiday when you’re stuck at home alone. And secondly, don’t judge by the horrific Netflix Adaptation; I couldn’t bear to watch half of it and deleted it just not to ruin the positive memories.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“You just spent a hell of a long time thinking up that quality comeback.”</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17678067023244637656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3063783482" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3063783482" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9314299-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417046774p2/9314299.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3063783482?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/9314299-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781101998618" href="/book/show/28953555-let-it-snow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9314299-jessica?shelf=teen-novels">teen-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9314299-jessica?shelf=christmas">christmas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9314299-jessica?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3063783482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9116519792419183957">I received this book for free from Penguin Teen for promotional purposes.<br/><br/>I was really excited to read this because I wanted to watch the movie on Netflix. For once, I was good and actually read the book first. I haven’t watched the movie yet but I will at some point in the next few days so my review is solely based on the book.<br/><br/>As a whole, I found this to be underwhelming. I had such high hopes but it didn’t quite reach them. This book was originally published in 2008 and I felt like this was a v</span>
  <span id="freeText9116519792419183957" style="display:none">I received this book for free from Penguin Teen for promotional purposes.<br /><br />I was really excited to read this because I wanted to watch the movie on Netflix. For once, I was good and actually read the book first. I haven’t watched the movie yet but I will at some point in the next few days so my review is solely based on the book.<br /><br />As a whole, I found this to be underwhelming. I had such high hopes but it didn’t quite reach them. This book was originally published in 2008 and I felt like this was a very typical YA book from that time. There was nothing that really drew me in and made me fall in love with it. I also didn’t feel any sort of attachment to the characters. I felt sort of meh about all of them. <br /><br />As for the three stories, the best one was The Jubilee Express, followed by The Patron Saint of Pigs and A Cheertastic Christmas Miracle. <br /><br />I did like that even though they were three separate stories, they still felt cohesive, as if they were all a part of the same novel. I liked that some of the characters crossed over into the other stories. That helped tie everything together nicely. <br /><br />Overall, this book wasn’t what I was expecting, but if want a cheesy YA romance to read for Christmas, give it a shot! </span>
  <a data-text-id="9116519792419183957" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

		    <b>
          <a title="Addicted to YA" class="actionLink" href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/2103616-let-it-snow">Addicted to YA:</a>
        </b>
      
			<a class="actionLink" href="/topic/show/2103616-let-it-snow">Let It Snow</a>
		</td>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BEuHxR4A/2aTJcfLPv+iaNHfIjm63ZSc6EYPhcV+cyc+be4XpV42DjQOc6rJCqi3B4DF8XRQGvuzOEk0CD2BvQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9ymIxq0lonKM0BCAnKIn32KNa4f6Lgey8bTLxygug9zND+EUFntrGiv7pOFrVy0AtNKMTzSjidWqyo125W1xRg==')})
  }
//]]>

As they explore the city that has become Mia\'s home, Adam and Mia revisit the past and open their hearts to the future - and each other.\n\nTold from Adam\'s point of view in the spare, lyrical prose that defined If I Stay, Where She Went explores the devastation of grief, the promise of new hope, and the flame of rekindled romance.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"2114232879977661758\" href=\"#\"           <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15504611851379301353"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br/><br/>John Green's first novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/99561.Looking_for_Alaska' title='Looking for Alaska by John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>Looking for Alaska</a>, won the 2006 Michael L. Printz Award presented by the American Library Association. His second novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49750.An_Abundance_of_Katherines' title='An Abundance of Katherines by John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>An Abundance of Katherines</a>, was a 2007 Michael L. Printz Award Honor Book and a finalist for the Los Angeles Times Book Prize. His next novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2914097.Paper_Towns' title='Paper Towns by John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>Paper Towns</a>, is a New </span>
  <span id="freeText15504611851379301353" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br /><br />John Green's first novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/99561.Looking_for_Alaska" title="Looking for Alaska by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Looking for Alaska</a>, won the 2006 Michael L. Printz Award presented by the American Library Association. His second novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49750.An_Abundance_of_Katherines" title="An Abundance of Katherines by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">An Abundance of Katherines</a>, was a 2007 Michael L. Printz Award Honor Book and a finalist for the Los Angeles Times Book Prize. His next novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2914097.Paper_Towns" title="Paper Towns by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Paper Towns</a>, is a New York Times bestseller and won the Edgar Allen Poe Award for Best YA Mystery. In January 2012, his most recent novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11870085.The_Fault_in_Our_Stars" title="The Fault in Our Stars by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fault in Our Stars</a>, was met with wide critical acclaim, unprecedented in Green's career. The praise included rave reviews in Time Magazine and The New York Times, on NPR, and from award-winning author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11466.Markus_Zusak" title="Markus Zusak" rel="nofollow noopener">Markus Zusak</a>. The book also topped the New York Times Children's Paperback Bestseller list for several weeks. Green has also coauthored a book with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11664.David_Levithan" title="David Levithan" rel="nofollow noopener">David Levithan</a> called <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6567017.Will_Grayson__Will_Grayson" title="Will Grayson, Will Grayson by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Will Grayson, Will Grayson</a>, published in 2010. The film rights for all his books, with the exception of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6567017.Will_Grayson__Will_Grayson" title="Will Grayson, Will Grayson by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Will Grayson Will Grayson</a>, have been optioned to major Hollywood Studios.<br /><br />In 2007, John and his brother Hank were the hosts of a popular internet blog, "<a href="http://www.brotherhood2.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Brotherhood 2.0</a>," where they discussed their lives, books and current events every day for a year except for weekends and holidays. They still keep a video blog, now called "The Vlog Brothers," which can be found on the <a href="http://nerdfighters.ning.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Nerdfighters</a> website, or a direct link <a href="http://youtube.com/vlogbrothers" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15504611851379301353" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
